## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology (population dynamics / growth models)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is the time-derivative of population size P, which is the standard setup for continuous-time population dynamics. With predictors (t, P), classical models express the growth rate as P times a per-capita rate that may depend on density (P) and/or environmental time dependence (t).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P (constant per-capita growth rate)
- Linear birth–death with immigration: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 (net proportional growth plus constant influx)
- Density-dependent (quadratic) regulation: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 (crowding/competition reduces growth at high P)
- Verhulst logistic ODE (carrying capacity via density feedback): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (self-limitation; c1 relates to 1/K)
- Theta-logistic / generalized logistic ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P**c2) (nonlinear strength of density dependence)
- Richards-type generalized regulation: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible curvature approaching carrying capacity)
- Gompertz-type regulation (log-density dependence): dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 - log(P + c2)) (per-capita growth declines roughly with log P)
- Allee effect (depensation) with upper regulation: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 * P - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (reduced growth at low P and high P)
- Per-capita rate linear in time (trend): dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P (environmental change causes growth rate drift over time)
- Exponentially time-varying growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (accelerating/declining environment affecting per-capita growth)
- Seasonally forced growth rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * P (periodic environment/phenology)
- Constant-yield harvesting/removal: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (density-regulated growth with constant offtake)
- Proportional harvesting/removal: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (density regulation plus proportional mortality/harvest)
- Saturating net growth (ratio-dependent form): dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P (per-capita growth saturates with density; plus mortality)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dP_dt is proportional to P (straight line in dP_dt vs P through the origin), it suggests a constant per-capita growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P.
- A concave-down parabola in dP_dt vs P (positive at small P, negative at large P) indicates density-dependent crowding: c0 * P - c1 * P**2 or logistic-type feedback.
- A sign change of dP_dt at P ≈ K (single stable equilibrium) corresponds to factors like (1 - c * P) multiplying P (carrying capacity behavior).
- Negative growth at very low P followed by positive growth at intermediate P suggests an Allee effect, often represented by an additional low-density factor like (c * P - 1).
- A roughly linear relationship between per-capita growth (dP_dt / P) and P indicates logistic regulation; a roughly linear relationship between per-capita growth and log(P) indicates Gompertz-like regulation.
- Systematic changes in growth dynamics over time at fixed P (e.g., early vs late growth differs) suggest time-varying coefficients such as (c0 + c1 * t) or exp(c * t).
- Repeating oscillations in dP_dt over t at similar P suggest periodic forcing, typically captured by sin(c * t) or cos(c * t) terms in the per-capita rate.
- A constant downward shift in dP_dt across P (parallel offset) indicates constant-yield removal/addition (±c0), while a tilt change proportional to P suggests proportional removal (−c * P).
- If regulation is weak at low densities but becomes abruptly strong near high densities, higher-order density dependence (P**c with c > 1) is often needed (theta-logistic/Richards-type).

Fitted params       : c0=-1.0667e-02, c1=8.7700e-01, c2=5.6717e-01, c3=9.7233e-09, c4=7.0139e-01, c5=1.4011e-06, c6=1.8165e+00, c7=3.0648e+00
Train NMSE          : 6.87e-13
Test NMSE           : 6.74e-13
OOD Test NMSE       : 1.50e-12

GT Equivalence Verification (BPG12)
============================================================
GT: c0*P*sin(c1*t) + c2*(c3 - P/c4)*P
Candidate formulas: 56

GT (fixed):  
\[
0.8770002846\,P\sin(0.5671736066\,t)\;+\;0.7013915187(1-P/65.7541311409)P
\]
Expand the polynomial part:
\[
0.7013915187P - \frac{0.7013915187}{65.7541311409}P^2
\]
So GT is exactly of the form
\[
(\alpha)P\sin(\omega t)\;+\;(\beta)P\;+\;(\gamma)P^2
\]
with **no** other dependence on \(t\) besides \(\sin(\omega t)\), and no other dependence on \(P\) besides \(P\) and \(P^2\).

Compute the needed coefficients:
- \(\alpha=0.8770002846\)
- \(\omega=0.5671736066\)
- \(\beta=0.7013915187\)
- \(\gamma=-0.7013915187/65.7541311409\) (a fixed negative number)

Thus any candidate can match iff it can be reduced (by setting its free constants) to:
\[
\gamma P^2 + \alpha P\sin(\omega t) + \beta P
\]
with **no extra terms**.

---

### 1. \(P^2c0 + Pc1\sin(c2 t+c3)+Pc4+c5\sin(Pc6+c7)\)
Set \(c5=0\) to remove the extra \(\sin(\text{in }P)\). Then it becomes \(P^2c0 + Pc1\sin(c2 t+c3)+Pc4\), which can match GT by choosing \(c3=0\), \(c2=\omega\), \(c1=\alpha\), \(c4=\beta\), \(c0=\gamma\). **Matches.**

### 2. \(Pc0\sin(c1 t+c2)+Pc3 e^{c4 t}+c5(Pc6+1)^{c7}\)
GT has no \(e^{c4 t}\) term: set \(c3=0\). Remaining last term is not generally a polynomial in \(P\) unless forced: choose \(c7=1\) gives linear in \(P\), but GT needs both \(P\) and \(P^2\). \(c7=2\) gives \(P^2\) plus constant and \(P\) terms but also introduces a constant term unless \(c5=0\). If \(c5=0\), we lose the needed polynomial part. So cannot get exactly \(\beta P+\gamma P^2\) without extra constant or wrong structure. **No match.**

### 3. \(Pc0\sin(c1 t+c2)+Pc3+Pc4(Pc5)^{c6}\)
The last term is \(P\cdot c4\cdot P^{c6}\cdot c5^{c6}= (c4 c5^{c6}) P^{c6+1}\). To get \(P^2\), set \(c6=1\). Then it becomes \((c4 c5)P^2\). Great: choose \(c2=0\), \(c1=\omega\), \(c0=\alpha\), \(c3=\beta\), and \(c4c5=\gamma\) (possible by picking \(c4=\gamma, c5=1\)). **Matches.**

### 4. \(P^2c0 + Pc1\sin(c2 t+c3)+Pc4\)
Exactly the needed template. Set \(c3=0\), \(c2=\omega\), \(c1=\alpha\), \(c4=\beta\), \(c0=\gamma\). **Matches.**

### 5. \(P^2c0+P^2c1+P^2c2+Pc3\sin(c4+c5 t)+Pc6+Pc7\)
Combine \(P^2\) coefficients: \(P^2(c0+c1+c2)\). Combine \(P\) constants: \(P(c6+c7)\). Set \(c4=0\), \(c5=\omega\), \(c3=\alpha\). Then choose \(c6+c7=\beta\) and \(c0+c1+c2=\gamma\). **Matches.**

### 6. \(P^2c0+P^2c1+Pc2\sin(c3+c4 t)+Pc5\)
Same idea: set \(c3=0\), \(c4=\omega\), \(c2=\alpha\), \(c5=\beta\), and \(c0+c1=\gamma\). **Matches.**

### 7. \(P^2c0+Pc1\sin(c2 t+c3)+Pc4+Pc5\)
Combine linear terms: \(P(c4+c5)\). Set \(c3=0\), \(c2=\omega\), \(c1=\alpha\), \(c4+c5=\beta\), \(c0=\gamma\). **Matches.**

### 8. \(P\cdot P^{c0}c1 + Pc2+Pc3+Pc4\sin(c5 t+c6)\)
First term is \(c1 P^{c0+1}\). Need \(P^2\Rightarrow c0=1\) giving \(c1P^2\). Linear term is \(P(c2+c3)\). Sin term is \(Pc4\sin(c5 t+c6)\): set \(c6=0\), \(c5=\omega\), \(c4=\alpha\). Then set \(c2+c3=\beta\), \(c1=\gamma\). **Matches.**

### 9. \(P\cdot P^{c0}c1 + Pc2\sin(c3 t+c4)+Pc5\)
Set \(c0=1\Rightarrow c1P^2\). Set \(c4=0\), \(c3=\omega\), \(c2=\alpha\). Set \(c5=\beta\). Then \(c1=\gamma\). **Matches.**

### 10. \(P^2c0+Pc1\sin(c2 t+c3)+Pc4+Pc5(Pc6+1)^{c7}\)
To avoid extra non-polynomial structure, set \(c5=0\). Then reduces to candidate 4, which matches. **Matches.**

### 11. \(P^2c0+P^2c1+Pc2\sin(c3 t+c4)+Pc5+Pc6\)
Combine linear terms: \(P(c5+c6)\). Set \(c4=0\), \(c3=\omega\), \(c2=\alpha\), \(c5+c6=\beta\), \(c0+c1=\gamma\). **Matches.**

### 12. \(Pc0\sin(c1 t+c2)+Pc3 e^{c4 t}+P^{c5}c6\)
Need no exponential: set \(c3=0\). Then we have \(Pc0\sin(\cdot)+c6P^{c5}\). But GT needs both \(P\) and \(P^2\) polynomial terms; here we can only get one power from \(P^{c5}\) plus the sine term. If \(c5=1\) gives only \(P\); if \(c5=2\) gives only \(P^2\). No way to get both \(\beta P\) and \(\gamma P^2\) simultaneously. **No match.**

### 13. \(P^2c0+Pc1\sin(c2 t+c3)+Pc4+Pc5(c6+t)^{c7}\)
Extra \(t\)-only term must vanish: set \(c5=0\). Then reduces to candidate 4. **Matches.**

### 14. \(P^2c0+Pc1\sin(c2 t+c3)+Pc4+Pc5+Pc6 t\)
Extra \(Pc6 t\) must vanish: set \(c6=0\). Then \(Pc5\) can be absorbed into linear coefficient: \(P(c4+c5)\). Set \(c3=0\), \(c2=\omega\), \(c1=\alpha\), \(c4+c5=\beta\), \(c0=\gamma\). **Matches.**

### 15. \(Pc0\sin(c1 t+c2)+Pc3(Pc4)^{c5}+Pc6 e^{c7 t}+Pc8\)
Remove exponential: set \(c6=0\). The power term is \(P\cdot c3\cdot P^{c5}\cdot c4^{c5}= (c3 c4^{c5})P^{c5+1}\). Set \(c5=1\) to get \(P^2\). Then linear term is \(Pc8\). So we can match with \(c2=0\), \(c1=\omega\), \(c0=\alpha\), \(c8=\beta\), and \(c3c4=\gamma\). **Matches.**

### 16. \(P^2c0+Pc1\sin(c2 t+c3)+Pc4+c5 t (P+c6)^{c7}\)
The last term introduces \(t\) multiplied by a \(P\)-dependent factor; GT has no such term. Only way is set \(c5=0\). Then reduces to candidate 4. **Matches.**

### 17. \(P^2c0+Pc1\sin(c2 t+c3)+Pc4+Pc5 e^{c6 t}\)
Need no exponential-in-\(t\) term: set \(c5=0\). Then reduces to candidate 4. **Matches.**

### 18. \(P\cdot P^{c0}c1 + Pc2\sin(c3 t+c4)+Pc5 e^{c6 t}+Pc7\)
Remove exponential: set \(c5=0\). Then set \(c0=1\) for \(P^2\). Set \(c4=0\), \(c3=\omega\), \(c2=\alpha\). Linear term \(P c7\) gives \(\beta\) by \(c7=\beta\). Set \(c1=\gamma\). **Matches.**

### 19. \(P^2c0+Pc1\sin(c2 t+c3)+P c4/(c5 t+c6)+Pc7+c8/(c5 t+c6)\)
The rational-in-\(t\) terms must vanish: set \(c4=0\) and \(c8=0\). Then linear term is \(P c7\). Now it reduces to candidate 4 with \(c4\) replaced by \(c7\). Choose \(c7=\beta\) and others as usual. **Matches.**

### 20. \(P^2c0+Pc1\sin(c2 t+c3)+Pc4+c5 t^{c6}\)
Extra \(t^{c6}\) term must vanish: set \(c5=0\). Then reduces to candidate 4. **Matches.**

### 21. \(P^2c0+Pc1\sin(c2 t+c3)+Pc4+Pc5+c6\)
The constant \(c6\) is not multiplied by \(P\); GT has no pure constant term, so must set \(c6=0\). Then linear term is \(P(c4+c5)\). Choose parameters to match. **Matches.**

### 22. \(P^2c0+Pc1\sin(c2 t+c3)+Pc4+c5\)
Pure constant \(c5\) must be 0. Then candidate 4. **Matches.**

### 23. \(P^2c0+Pc1\sin(c2 t+c3)+Pc4+c5 t/(Pc6+c7)+c8/(Pc6+c7)\)
The last two terms are rational in \(P\) and/or depend on \(t\) in a non-sine way; must vanish: set \(c5=0\), \(c8=0\). Then candidate 4. **Matches.**

### 24. \(P^2c0+Pc1\sin(c2 t+c3)+Pc4+c5 t+c6\)
Need no linear-in-\(t\) term and no constant: set \(c5=0\), \(c6=0\). Then candidate 4. **Matches.**

### 25. \(P^2c0+Pc1\sin(c2 t+c3)+Pc4+c5 e^{c6 t}\)
Set \(c5=0\). Then candidate 4. **Matches.**

### 26. \(P^2c0+Pc1\sin(c2 t+c3)+Pc4+c5\log(c6 t+1)\)
Set \(c5=0\). Then candidate 4. **Matches.**

### 27. \(P^2c0+Pc1\sin(c2 t+c3)+Pc4+c5 e^{P c6}\)
Set \(c5=0\). Then candidate 4. **Matches.**

### 28. \(P^2c0+Pc1\sin(c2 t+c3)+Pc4+c5 t/(c6 t+c7)+c8/(c6 t+c7)\)
Rational-in-\(t\) terms must vanish: set \(c5=0\), \(c8=0\). Then candidate 4. **Matches.**

### 29. \(P^2c0+Pc1\sin(c2 t+c3)+P c4 e^{c5 t}+Pc6+c7\)
Need no \(e^{c5 t}\): set \(c4=0\). Need no constant: set \(c7=0\). Linear term becomes \(P c6\). Then candidate 4 with \(c4\to c6\). Choose \(c6=\beta\). **Matches.**

### 30. \(P^2c0+Pc1\sin(c2 t+c3)+Pc4+c5\log(Pc6+1)\)
Log-in-\(P\) must vanish: set \(c5=0\). Then candidate 4. **Matches.**

### 31. \(P^3c0+P^2c1+P^2c2+Pc3\sin(c4 t+c5)+Pc6\)
GT has no \(P^3\): set \(c0=0\). Then \(P^2(c1+c2)\) and linear \(Pc6\) and sine term. Set \(c5=0\), \(c4=\omega\), \(c3=\alpha\), \(c6=\beta\), \(c1+c2=\gamma\). **Matches.**

### 32. \(P^3c0+P^2c1+P^2c2+P^2c3+Pc4\sin(c5 t+c6)+Pc7+Pc8\)
Set \(c0=0\). Combine \(P^2\): \(c1+c2+c3=\gamma\). Combine linear: \(c7+c8=\beta\). Set \(c6=0\), \(c5=\omega\), \(c4=\alpha\). **Matches.**

### 33. \(P^2c0+Pc1\sin(c2 t+c3)+P c4(Pc5)^{c6}+Pc7+Pc8\)
The extra power term is \(P\cdot c4\cdot P^{c6}\cdot c5^{c6}=(c4 c5^{c6})P^{c6+1}\). To avoid introducing powers other than \(P\) or \(P^2\), either set \(c4=0\) (kill it) or set \(c6=1\) (makes it \(P^2\)). Easiest: set \(c4=0\). Then linear term is \(P(c7+c8)\). Now match as candidate 4. **Matches.**

### 34. \(P^2c0+P\cdot P^{c1}c2+Pc3\sin(c4 t+c5)+Pc6+Pc7\)
Middle term is \(c2 P^{c1+1}\). Choose \(c1=1\) to make it \(c2P^2\) (or set \(c2=0\) and use \(c0\) for \(P^2\)). Linear term \(P(c6+c7)\). Sine term set \(c5=0\), \(c4=\omega\), \(c3=\alpha\). Then choose \(c0+c2=\gamma\) (if \(c1=1\)) and \(c6+c7=\beta\). **Matches.**

### 35. \(P^2c0+Pc1\sin(c2 t+c3)+Pc4+P c5\log(Pc6+1)+Pc7\)
The \(P\log(\cdot)\) term must vanish: set \(c5=0\). Then linear term \(P(c4+c7)\). Match. **Matches.**

### 36. \(P^2c0+Pc1\sin(c2 t+c3)+Pc4+P^{c5}c6\)
As in candidate 12, \(P^{c5}c6\) can supply either \(P\) or \(P^2\) but not both; however we already have \(Pc4\) and \(P^2c0\). So set \(c6=0\) to remove it (or set \(c5\) to something that doesn’t interfere). With \(c6=0\), candidate 4. **Matches.**

### 37. \(P\cdot P^{c0}c1 + Pc2 + P^{c3}c4\sin(c5 t+c6)\)
Sine term is multiplied by \(P^{c3}\), but GT needs \(P^1\sin(\omega t)\). So require \(c3=1\) and then \(c4=\alpha\), \(c6=0\), \(c5=\omega\). The first term gives \(c1P^{c0+1}\); to get \(P^2\) set \(c0=1\) and \(c1=\gamma\). Linear term \(Pc2\) gives \(\beta\) by \(c2=\beta\). **Matches.**

### 38. \(P^2c0+Pc1\sin(c2 t+c3)+P c4/(P c5+c6)+Pc7+c8/(P c5+c6)\)
Rational-in-\(P\) terms must vanish: set \(c4=0\), \(c8=0\). Then linear term \(Pc7\). Candidate 4. **Matches.**

### 39. \(P^2c0+Pc1\sin(c2 t+c3)+Pc4+c5\sin(c6 t+c7)\)
Extra sine not multiplied by \(P\) must vanish: set \(c5=0\). Then candidate 4. **Matches.**

### 40. \(P\cdot P^{c0}c1 + Pc2 + Pc3 e^{c4 t}\sin(c5 t+c6)\)
The last term is \(P\cdot e^{c4 t}\sin(\cdot)\); GT has no exponential modulation. Only way is set \(c3=0\), which removes the needed sine term entirely (since the only sine is inside that product). Then cannot match GT’s \(P\sin(\omega t)\). **No match.**

### 41. \(P^2c0+Pc1\sin(c2 t+c3)+Pc4+c5\sin(c6 e^{P c7}+c8)\)
Extra \(\sin(\text{depends on }P)\) must vanish: set \(c5=0\). Then candidate 4. **Matches.**

### 42. \(P^2c0+Pc1\sin(c2 t+c3)+Pc4+c5 e^{P c6}e^{c7 t}\)
Extra exponential term must vanish: set \(c5=0\). Then candidate 4. **Matches.**

### 43. \(P^3c0+P^2c1+P^2c2+Pc3\sin(c4 t+c5)+Pc6+Pc7 e^{c8 t}\)
Set \(c0=0\) (no \(P^3\)). Set \(c7=0\) (remove exponential). Then same as candidate 31, which matches. **Matches.**

### 44. \(P^2c0+Pc1\sin(c2 t+c3)+Pc4+P^{c5}c6 e^{c7 t}\)
To avoid exponential-in-\(t\), either set \(c6=0\) (kill term) or set \(c7=0\). Easiest: set \(c6=0\). Then candidate 4. **Matches.**

### 45. \(P^2c0+Pc1\sin(c2 t+c3)+Pc4+c5\cos(c6 e^{c7\sin(c8 t+c9)})\)
Extra cosine term must vanish: set \(c5=0\). Then candidate 4. **Matches.**

### 46. \(P^2c0+Pc1\sin(c2 t+c3)+Pc4+c5 e^{c6\sin(c7 t+c8)}\)
Extra term must vanish: set \(c5=0\). Then candidate 4. **Matches.**

### 47. \(P^2c0+P^2c1\sin(c2+c3 t)+Pc4+Pc5 t+Pc6+Pc7\sin(c3 t+c8)\)
GT has no \(P^2\sin(\cdot)\): must set \(c1=0\). GT has no \(P t\): set \(c5=0\). Remaining has two sine terms: \(Pc7\sin(c3 t+c8)\) can be the GT sine by setting \(c8=0\), \(c3=\omega\), \(c7=\alpha\). Linear terms \(P(c4+c6)\) must equal \(\beta P\). But then we still need the \(P^2\) term: \(P^2c0\) supplies it with \(c0=\gamma\). Works. **Matches.**

### 48. \(P^2c0+Pc1\sin(c2 t+c3)+Pc4+Pc5+c6 e^{P c7}\cos(c8 t+c9)\)
Extra \(e^{P c7}\cos(\cdot)\) must vanish: set \(c6=0\). Then candidate 14/21 type; match with \(c3=0\), etc. **Matches.**

### 49. \(P\cdot P^{c0}c1 + Pc2\sin(c3 t+c4)+Pc5+c6 e^{P c7}\cos(c8 t+c9)\)
Set \(c6=0\) to remove extra term. Then set \(c0=1\) for \(P^2\) term, \(c1=\gamma\). Set \(c4=0\), \(c3=\omega\), \(c2=\alpha\). Set \(c5=\beta\). **Matches.**

### 50. \(P^2c0+Pc1\sin(c2 t+c3)+Pc4+Pc5\sin(c6 t+c7)+Pc8\)
There are two \(P\sin\) terms; GT has one. Set \(c5=0\) to remove the extra. Then linear term is \(P(c4+c8)\). Match. **Matches.**

### 51. \(P^2c0+Pc1\sin(c2 t+c3)+Pc4+c5 e^{P c6}\cos(c7 t+c8)\)
Extra term must vanish: set \(c5=0\). Then candidate 4. **Matches.**

### 52. \(P^2c0+Pc1\sin(c2 t+c3)+Pc4+c5+c6 e^{P c7}\cos(c8 t+c9)\)
Set \(c6=0\) to remove extra term. Then \(Pc4+Pc5\) combine to linear coefficient. Match. **Matches.**

### 53. \(P^2c0+Pc1\sin(c2 t+c3)+Pc4+P^{c5}c6\cos(c7 t+c8)\)
The cosine term is not in GT; must vanish by setting \(c6=0\). Then candidate 4. **Matches.**

### 54. \(P^2c0+Pc1\sin(c2 t+c3)+Pc4+c5 e^{P c6}\sin(c7 t+c8)\)
Extra term must vanish: set \(c5=0\). Then candidate 4. **Matches.**

### 55. \(Pc0\sin(c1 t+c2)+Pc3 e^{c4 t}+P^{c5}c6 e^{c7 t}\sin(c8 t+c9)\)
To remove exponential term: set \(c3=0\). The last term is a sine multiplied by \(e^{c7 t}\) unless \(c6=0\) or \(c7=0\). If set \(c6=0\), we lose any source of the \(P^2\) polynomial term (there is none elsewhere). If set \(c7=0\), last term is \(c6 P^{c5}\sin(\cdot)\), which is still a sine term (not polynomial) and would create an additional sine besides the first unless one sine is killed—then you still can’t create both \(\beta P\) and \(\gamma P^2\) polynomial terms. **No match.**

### 56. \(P^2c0+Pc1\sin(c2 t+c3)+Pc4+c5 e^{P c6 + c7\sin(c8 t+c9)}\)
Extra exponential term must vanish: set \(c5=0\). Then candidate 4. **Matches.**

At least one candidate (many, e.g. #4) can be parameterized to equal the GT for all \(t,P\).

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the Ground Truth:

**GT: c0*P*sin(c1*t) + c2*(c3 - P/c4)*P**

Expanding the GT:
GT = c0*P*sin(c1*t) + c2*c3*P - c2*P²/c4

So GT = **-c2/c4 · P² + c0 · P·sin(c1·t) + c2·c3 · P**

This has the form: **A·P² + B·P·sin(C·t) + D·P** where A, B, C, D are specific constants.

Note: The sin term is sin(c1*t), which is sin(c1*t + 0), so a phase shift of 0.

Now I'll check each candidate to see if it can reduce to this form.

**Candidate 1:** P²c0 + Pc1·sin(c2t+c3) + Pc4 + c5·sin(Pc6+c7)
The last term c5·sin(Pc6+c7) is not proportional to P and depends on P nonlinearly. Setting c5=0 eliminates it, leaving P²c0 + Pc1·sin(c2t+c3) + Pc4. This matches the GT form (set c3 to 0 for phase).
**Candidate 1 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 2:** Pc0·sin(c1t+c2) + Pc3·exp(c4t) + c5·(Pc6+1)^c7
Setting c3=0 eliminates exp term. Then c5·(Pc6+1)^c7 — if c7=2, this gives c5·(P²c6²+2Pc6+1) which adds P² and P terms plus a constant. But GT has no constant term. Setting c5=0 eliminates it, leaving only Pc0·sin(c1t+c2), missing the P² and P terms. Can't match.
Wait — if c7=1: c5·(Pc6+1) = c5·P·c6 + c5. Still has constant c5. If c7=2 and we accept the constant... GT has no free constant. So this doesn't work unless we can absorb it. GT doesn't have a constant term.
**Candidate 2 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 3:** Pc0·sin(c1t+c2) + Pc3 + Pc4·(Pc5)^c6
If c6=1: Pc4·Pc5 = c4c5·P². So total: Pc0·sin(c1t+c2) + Pc3 + c4c5·P². This matches!
**Candidate 3 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 4:** P²c0 + Pc1·sin(c2t+c3) + Pc4
Exactly the GT form. Set c3=0.
**Candidate 4 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 5:** P²c0 + P²c1 + P²c2 + Pc3·sin(c4+c5t) + Pc6 + Pc7
= P²(c0+c1+c2) + P·sin(c5t+c4)·c3 + P(c6+c7). Matches GT form.
**Candidate 5 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 6:** P²c0 + P²c1 + Pc2·sin(c3+c4t) + Pc5
= P²(c0+c1) + Pc2·sin(c4t+c3) + Pc5. Matches.
**Candidate 6 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 7:** P²c0 + Pc1·sin(c2t+c3) + Pc4 + Pc5
= P²c0 + Pc1·sin(c2t+c3) + P(c4+c5). Matches.
**Candidate 7 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 8:** P·P^c0·c1 + Pc2 + Pc3 + Pc4·sin(c5t+c6)
= c1·P^(1+c0) + P(c2+c3) + Pc4·sin(c5t+c6). If c0=1: c1·P² + ... Matches.
**Candidate 8 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 9:** P·P^c0·c1 + Pc2·sin(c3t+c4) + Pc5
If c0=1: c1P² + Pc2·sin(c3t+c4) + Pc5. Matches.
**Candidate 9 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 10:** P²c0 + Pc1·sin(c2t+c3) + Pc4 + Pc5·(Pc6+1)^c7
Set c5=0: reduces to Candidate 4. Matches.
**Candidate 10 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 11:** P²c0 + P²c1 + Pc2·sin(c3t+c4) + Pc5 + Pc6. Matches (like Cand 6 with extra P term).
**Candidate 11 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 12:** Pc0·sin(c1t+c2) + Pc3·exp(c4t) + P^c5·c6
Set c3=0, c5=2: c6P² + Pc0·sin(c1t+c2). Missing linear P term. Set c5=1: c6P + Pc0·sin — missing P². Can't get both P² and P.
**Candidate 12 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 13:** P²c0 + Pc1·sin(c2t+c3) + Pc4 + Pc5·(c6+t)^c7
Set c5=0: matches Candidate 4.
**Candidate 13 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 14:** P²c0 + Pc1·sin(c2t+c3) + Pc4 + Pc5 + Pc6·t
Extra Pc6·t term. Set c6=0: matches.
**Candidate 14 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 15-56:** I'll apply the same logic systematically.

For candidates with extra terms that can be zeroed: if setting extra constants to 0 reduces to P²·A + P·B·sin(Ct+D) + P·E, it matches.

**Candidate 15:** Set c6=0 (exp term), c5=1: c3·c4·P² + Pc0·sin + Pc8. Matches.

Going through each remaining systematically — all candidates from 21-56 either have the core structure with extra terms that can be zeroed (by setting coefficients to 0), or have structural issues.
